## DEC-066 — Originating Club FK target = Club entity; locked one-shot via OriginatingClubLocked event (2026-05-03)
- **Context**: Surfaced during Wave 1 Module K elicitation. Q-CL-3 ([`../03-qa/qa.modK.md`](../03-qa/qa.modK.md)) asked for the FK target of the Originating Club mechanic locked by DEC-008. Q-AD-12 asked for the lock event mechanic. Paolo confirmed Interpretation A on Q-CL-3 and confirmed the OriginatingClubLocked event on Q-AD-12.
- **Decision**:
  - **FK target**: `Customer.originating_club_id` → `Club.club_id` (Module K §6.6). The Originating Club is semantically the *Club* (per BMD §0.4 / §2.2 wording: "first-approved club"); the eventual settlement recipient (Producer) is found via deref to `Club.partner_producer_id`.
  - **Lock mechanism**: a one-shot `OriginatingClubLocked` event fires at the Customer's *first* `MembershipApprovedByProducer` across any club, gated on `Customer.originating_club_id IS NULL`. Once set, the field is immutable in the application layer (no admin override surface at launch).
  - **Event payload**: `customer_id`, `club_id`, `locked_at`, `triggering_membership_id` (for audit).
  - **Closed-Club edge case**: a Club with `status = closed` still resolves cleanly to its Producer because v17 §6.6 makes `Club.partner_producer_id` immutable once set; settlement deref works regardless of Club lifecycle state.
  - **No-OC allowance**: per DEC-040, a Customer who buys on Discovery without ever joining a Club may have `originating_club_id = NULL` indefinitely; the 5% × `P_d` Originating-Club share simply does not accrue for those purchases.
- **Implications**:
  - **Module K PRD draft (Wave 1)**: Customer entity field added (`originating_club_id` nullable FK); event added to §6.17 set.
  - **Module E settlement (Wave 5)**: Originating-Club share computed by joining Customer → Club → Producer; one indexed deref per Discovery sale.
  - **Multi-Club-per-Producer (BMD §3.4)**: a Producer with multiple Clubs sees the Originating Club resolved at Club level (the *specific* Club that approved the Customer), not aggregated to the Producer; Producer-side reporting can group across their Clubs if useful.
- **Amends / supersedes**: DEC-008 (refines the FK target without changing the mechanic). DEC-040 (no-OC purchase remains the explicit NULL allowance).
- **BMD revision**: none — BMD §2.2 / §0.4 already lock the mechanic in prose; the FK choice is a PRD-implementation detail.
- **Owner**: Paolo.
- **Stage 6.5 clarification (2026-05-08, E6-47)**: Originating Club FK preservation through gifting → burn → settlement chain. A Voucher's `originating_club_id` lineage preserves through gifting (DEC-116 transfers the Voucher; OC binding follows the original purchaser per OC immutability). Through burn (Module B `BottleNFTBurned`) and settlement (Module E quarter-end OC settlement read), the originating_club_id remains bound to the original purchase event for accrual / reversal computation. Anchored at Module S §11.5 + Module B §6 + Module E quarter-end OC settlement; closes E6-47 (OC dimension).

---

## DEC-067 — Producer ≠ Supplier separation carries forward verbatim from v17; Supplier-operated Clubs flagged as future flexibility (2026-05-03)
- **Context**: Surfaced during Wave 1 Module K elicitation. Q-CL-4 asked whether NewCo collapses Producer + Supplier (BMD §3.1 silent on Supplier; suggests simpler reality) or carries v17's separation forward. Paolo confirmed Interpretation A and added: "for the Discovery business, NewCo will deal with Suppliers (that are not Producers) as well as Producers. True that for the club business NewCo will deal with Producers, but maybe a Supplier will want his own Club as well. So: the separation and relationships survive."
- **Decision**:
  - **Carry v17 forward verbatim**: Module K retains both Producer Registry (§6.3a) and Party Registry with `party_type = SUPPLIER` (§6.3); SupplierProducerLink (Module D §3.10) is implemented in Wave 2; explicit operator action is required to link a Supplier to one or more Producers (no auto-link per v17 §6.3a rule 2).
  - **Discovery side at launch**: NewCo deals with both Producers (who make wine) and Suppliers (who supply wine but may not produce it themselves — e.g., Crurated as a Discovery supplier per DEC-020). The Producer ≠ Supplier separation is therefore an active operational reality at launch, not just inheritance discipline.
  - **Club side at launch**: Clubs are Producer-operated (`Club.partner_producer_id` FK to Producer; v17 §6.6 unchanged). All NewCo launch Clubs anchor to a Producer.
  - **Future-flexibility note (NOT a launch decision)**: Paolo flagged that a Supplier may want to operate their own Club post-launch. The current `Club.partner_producer_id` FK does not admit Supplier-operated Clubs directly. If/when this materialises, a future-DEC item will generalise the Club-operator FK (e.g., polymorphic `operator_party_id` + `operator_party_type` enum, or a parallel `partner_supplier_id` FK with a one-or-the-other constraint). **Not in launch scope.**
- **Implications**:
  - **Module K PRD draft (Wave 1)**: documents Producer Registry + Supplier (Party with `party_type = SUPPLIER`) entities and their relationship via SupplierProducerLink, citing v17 §6.3 / §6.3a / §3.10 by section number. Notes the future-flexibility carve-out for Supplier-operated Clubs.
  - **Operational note**: 95%+ of NewCo Producers will have a 1:1 SupplierProducerLink at launch; the separation is preserved for the edge cases (champagne house distributed via holding entity; producer with separate négociant arm) and for inheritance discipline.
- **Amends / supersedes**: none. Operationalises BMD Appendix B.1 (Producer ≠ Supplier kept).
- **BMD revision**: optional minor — a Glossary entry distinguishing Producer (wine identity) from Supplier (commercial counterpart) would help readers; v0.4 consolidator's call. The Supplier-operated-Club future-flexibility note is a Module K PRD concern, not BMD-level. **Deferred to v0.4 consolidation queue.**
- **Owner**: Paolo.

---

## DEC-068 — B2B segment dropped at Customer level; company-billing details preserved at Address / Payment-method level for individual collectors (2026-05-03)
- **Context**: Surfaced during Wave 1 Module K elicitation. Q-AD-1 asked whether NewCo Customer entity drops `customer_type` enum and all B2B-specific fields (per DEC-017 — no B2B at launch). Paolo confirmed dropping B2B-as-segment but flagged: "it is possible that collectors choose to register / sign up with their own companies, mainly for their own fiscal reasons outside our ERP (e.g., company billing address, use of company credit cards)."
- **Decision**:
  - **B2B as a customer segment is OUT** (per DEC-017, BMD §13.2): no `customer_type` enum on Customer; no B2B-specific Customer fields (`legal_entity_type`, `registration_number`, `primary_contact_name/email`); every NewCo Customer at launch is conceptually B2C (an individual collector). NewCo does not sell to restaurants, hospitality businesses, or other B2B segments.
  - **Company-billing affordance is IN**: an individual collector may transact using company billing details for their own fiscal reasons. Implementation:
    - **Address entity** (Module K): `BillingAddress` rows can carry optional `company_name` and `vat_id` fields. The Customer remains the natural-person; the Address attaches the legal-entity-on-receipt info.
    - **Payment-method records** (Module E + Stripe scope, Wave 5): a payment method may be a corporate credit card without altering the Customer's B2C classification.
  - **Invoicing**: when a Customer transacts using a company-billing Address, the invoice (INV1 / INV2 per DEC-045) is issued to the company entity (name, VAT ID); the underlying customer record stays the natural person. Module E owns the invoicing mechanic (Wave 5).
- **Implications**:
  - **Module K PRD draft (Wave 1)**: Customer entity is B2C-only; Address entity supports optional `company_name` + `vat_id`. The "B2B-as-segment" v17 fields (`customer_type` enum, B2B-specific fields) are **not** carried forward.
  - **Module E PRD (Wave 5)**: invoicing logic must read company-billing data from the Address used at purchase, not from a Customer-level `customer_type` flag. Wave 5 design point flagged here.
  - **Operational delta vs full B2B**: NewCo will not provide B2B-specific surfaces at launch (no wholesale catalog, no business-tier pricing, no purchase-order workflow); only the billing/invoicing affordance to support individual collectors using their own companies.
- **Amends / supersedes**: refines DEC-017 (no B2B at launch) — clarifies that "no B2B" means "no B2B segment / surface", not "no company-billing affordance".
- **BMD revision**: none — BMD §13.2 stance ("B2B is OUT") is unchanged in scope; this DEC clarifies the implementation boundary at Customer-vs-Address level.
- **Owner**: Paolo.

---

## DEC-069 — Hero Package Allocation `qty` is mutable mid-year; producers can scale capacity, waitlist applicants gain eligibility on increase (2026-05-03)
- **Context**: Surfaced during Wave 1 Module K elicitation. Q-AD-7 asked about the Producer Portal capacity invariant (`# active Profiles ≤ qty(Hero Package allocation)`). Paolo confirmed the invariant and added: "make sure however that # of packages and therefore allowed members can change during the year. A producer launches the club for year 202x with 50 packages, after 3 months he is sold out and decides to make available additional 20 packages for 20 more members. This is possible."
- **Decision**:
  - **Allocation `qty` is mutable mid-year**: the Hero Package's underlying Allocation `qty` (Module A) is not frozen at year-start; the producer may increase it during the club year to admit additional members.
  - **Capacity invariant is evaluated against current qty**: `count(active Profiles for club X) ≤ Allocation.qty (current value, not year-start value)`. Lapsed / Cancelled Profiles do not count against the cap.
  - **Producer Portal surface**: in addition to "design Hero Package for year N" (initial creation), the surface exposes "increase capacity" affordance — a producer can add N more packages to the year's allocation. This is a Module A operation (`AllocationQtyAdjusted` event from v17 §2.1 or equivalent) that Module K listens to in order to re-evaluate the capacity invariant for waitlist conversions.
  - **Waitlist conversion on capacity increase**: when allocation `qty` increases by N, the producer (or platform, depending on policy) is offered N waitlisted applicants in priority order to approve. **Priority order is producer-discretionary at launch** (no automatic FIFO conversion); the producer reviews the waitlist and approves up to the new capacity.
  - **Decrease is constrained**: producers cannot reduce `qty` below the current count of active Profiles (would orphan members). Reductions above current count (e.g., 50 → 45 when only 40 active) are admitted but rare; a future-DEC may tighten this.
- **Implications**:
  - **Module K PRD draft (Wave 1)**: capacity invariant is a runtime check on the current `Allocation.qty`, not a stored field. The waitlist-conversion-on-increase mechanic is documented; priority order is producer-discretionary.
  - **Module A PRD (Wave 2)**: Allocation entity supports mid-year `qty` adjustments via existing v17 §2.1 mechanics; emits adjustment event consumed by Module K.
  - **Producer Portal UX (post-launch)**: surface for "increase capacity" affordance + waitlist review/approval flow.
  - **Future-flexibility note**: more sophisticated waitlist mechanics (FIFO auto-conversion, priority by application date, producer-defined ranking) are not in launch scope; flagged for post-launch consideration.
- **Amends / supersedes**: refines DEC-007 (`# of members = # of Hero Packages`) — clarifies that the Hero Package count is a *current-state* value, not a year-start commitment.
- **BMD revision**: §2.3 (where the "# of members = # of Hero Packages" invariant is locked) should add a sentence clarifying that the count is mutable mid-year. **Deferred to Wave-1-end BMD v0.4 consolidation.**
- **Owner**: Paolo.

---

## DEC-070 — Producer agreement = separate `ProducerAgreement` entity in Module K (Path Y) (2026-05-03)
- **Context**: Surfaced during Wave 1 Module K elicitation. Q-AD-9 asked for the placement of producer agreement metadata: fields on Producer (Path X), separate `ProducerAgreement` entity (Path Y), or external-doc reference (Path Z). Paolo confirmed Path Y.
- **Decision**:
  - **`ProducerAgreement` entity** in Module K, with `producer_id` FK and lifecycle (`draft / active / superseded / terminated`); carries term dates, settlement cadence, minimum allocation commitment, payment terms, and special-clause references.
  - **Multiple agreements over time**: a Producer may have a sequence of ProducerAgreement rows (initial 24-month + renewal 24-month + amendment); only one is `active` at any given time per Producer.
  - **Multi-brand / multi-Club producers (BMD §3.4)**: a Producer with multiple brands may have brand-specific sub-agreements via either (a) one ProducerAgreement covering all brands or (b) multiple ProducerAgreement rows scoped per Club. Both shapes admitted at launch; producer-by-producer call.
  - **Pattern precedent**: v17 §6.3b has `AgencyAgreement` as a similar producer-relationship-scoped entity; ProducerAgreement follows that pattern (rename if legal terminology differs at PRD time).
- **Implications**:
  - **Module K PRD draft (Wave 1)**: introduces `ProducerAgreement` entity with the field list above (placeholder until Q-OQ-9 template lands).
  - **Module D (Wave 2 / Wave 6)**: agreement-renewal workflow consumes ProducerAgreement state; transitions are owned by Module K.
  - **Settlement (Module E, Wave 5)**: settlement-cadence override per producer (DEC-042) reads from `ProducerAgreement.settlement_cadence`; default is the BMD-locked cadence.
  - **Q-OQ-9 dependency**: when the 24-month producer agreement template lands (per Q-OQ-9), the field list is finalised in a follow-up PRD revision.
- **Amends / supersedes**: none. Operationalises BMD §3.3 (24-month default term, settlement cadence, minimum allocation commitment) at the data-model level.
- **BMD revision**: none — BMD §3.3 already lists the metadata; this DEC picks the placement.
- **Owner**: Paolo.

---

## DEC-071 — Sanctions screening on Customer: separate enum + nullable fields; screening mandatory by application logic, not schema constraint (2026-05-03)
- **Context**: Surfaced during Wave 1 Module K elicitation. Q-AD-15 asked whether sanctions screening (EU + UIF + OFAC per DEC-030 / DEC-041) gets a separate `sanctions_status` enum on Customer or folds into the existing `kyc_status`. Paolo confirmed separate enum and added: "make sure these are optional and not mandatory."
- **Decision**:
  - **Separate enum**: `Customer.sanctions_status` with values (`pending / passed / failed / under_review`), distinct from `kyc_status`.
  - **Timestamps**: `Customer.sanctions_screened_at`, `Customer.next_rescreen_at` (12-month re-screening cadence per DEC-030).
  - **Nullability**: all three fields are nullable on Customer. Customers may exist with no screening record (e.g., before onboarding completes, admin-created records, imported legacy data). The schema does not enforce non-null.
  - **Screening enforcement is application-layer**: the BMD-locked policy (DEC-030 + DEC-041) — sanctions screening must complete before Customer can purchase — is enforced by application/business logic checking `sanctions_status = passed` before order completion. Schema does not block creation of unscreened Customer rows.
- **Implications**:
  - **Module K PRD draft (Wave 1)**: Customer entity adds the three fields as nullable; lifecycle events `CustomerOnboardingScreeningPassed/Failed`, `CustomerRescreeningPassed/Failed` (BMD §2.8) attach to this state.
  - **Application logic**: order-completion path (Module S, Wave 3) checks `Customer.sanctions_status = passed` as a precondition; rejects with screening-required error otherwise.
  - **Operational practice**: NewCo's onboarding flow runs sanctions screening synchronously during Customer creation; the nullable design accommodates exceptional paths (admin import, support-team manual creation) without schema rework.
- **Amends / supersedes**: none. Implements DEC-030 + DEC-041 at the Customer-entity field level.
- **BMD revision**: none — BMD §2.8 / §10.7 lock the screening policy; this DEC picks the implementation shape.
- **Owner**: Paolo.

---

## DEC-072 — BMD and PRD scope: event-determining, not accounting-policy-determining; accounting integration decides GL treatment (2026-05-03)
- **Context**: Raised by Paolo 2026-05-03 in response to BMD v0.4 §3.7 / §5.1 prose (added in v0.4 per DEC-063) that took positions on accounting treatment ("NewCo recognises the inventory liability on its balance sheet at purchase time"; "cost-of-goods recognition timing flips for direct-purchase batches"). Paolo articulated a general rule: "BMD and PRD do not take position or imply directly any accounting policy or how to treat an event from an accounting standpoint. Role is to determine the event, send the event to the accounting integrated software that is responsible to decide if an event triggers a balance sheet or P&L transaction etc."
- **Decision**: The BMD and PRD documents (across all modules and waves) **do not take positions on accounting policy** and **do not imply how to treat an event from an accounting standpoint**:
  - **BMD / PRD role**: determine the business / domain event (what happened, when, with what data); emit the event to the accounting integration.
  - **Accounting integration role** (Xero per DEC-028, with the Italian SDI connector): receive the event and decide whether and how it triggers a balance-sheet entry, P&L transaction, tax record, deferred revenue, etc. — per the accounting software's configured policies.
  - **Vocabulary discipline**: BMD / PRD prose may use accounting-domain *terminology* descriptively (e.g., "settlement", "invoice", "payment", "title transfer") but must not assert accounting *treatment* (e.g., "recognised on the balance sheet", "P&L recognition timing", "asset vs liability classification", "COGS timing", "deferred revenue", "revenue recognition under IFRS 15", etc.).
  - **Module E specifically** (the financial-event recorder, Wave 5): records the events and forwards them; does NOT specify GL treatment. Reinforces and generalises the existing Module E boundary principle (memory: `project_module_e_boundary.md`).
- **Implications**:
  - **BMD v0.4 same-day patch (2026-05-03)**: §3.7 and §5.1 direct-purchase prose reframed to event-only language. DEC-072 folded into §12.1; §0.14 + Reading-Guide DEC count + §12 intro updated to DEC-001..DEC-072.
  - **DEC-063**: the Module E implication clause restated in event-determining terms (no balance-sheet / COGS claims).
  - **All future BMD revisions and PRD drafts**: scrub for accounting-policy claims; replace with event-level descriptions ("event X fires at moment Y with payload Z; downstream accounting integration determines treatment").
  - **Existing v0.3 BMD §8 Monetization sections** (Revenue Recognition, MPV VAT mechanics, Producer Settlement accounting framing, etc.) inherit accounting-domain framing from earlier work that may already violate this rule. **NOT in scope of the v0.4 patch.** A future-DEC item can request a §8 sweep at Paolo's call.
- **Amends / supersedes**: reinforces and generalises the existing Module E boundary principle (Crurated v17 memory `project_module_e_boundary.md` — Module E records financial events; Xero decides GL treatment). Does not amend any prior NewCo DEC, but reframes the accounting-flavoured implications language in DEC-063.
- **BMD revision**: v0.4 same-day patch (no version bump — v0.4 not yet signed off): §3.7 + §5.1 direct-purchase prose reframed; DEC-072 folded into §12.1 + §0.14 + §12 intro + Reading-Guide. Optional broader §8 sweep flagged for future-DEC.
- **Owner**: Paolo.

---

## DEC-073 — PRD scope = product specs translating BMD into module behaviour; tech-implementation decisions are downstream (2026-05-03)
- **Context**: Surfaced 2026-05-03 in response to Module 0 / Module K v0.1 PRD drafting. Paolo flagged that the v0.1 drafts drifted into tech-implementation detail (JSON shape blocks, schema field tables with column types and nullability, FK column naming, exact-string enum specs, validation-placement claims). The general rule he articulated: "BMD is the business doc; the PRD translates the BMD into product specs — informative and clear for tech (and Claude Code) to then move into dev phase, but not strict on tech decisions like the JSON shape." Methodology DEC parallel to DEC-060 (inheritance) and DEC-072 (no accounting policy).
- **Decision**: NewCo PRDs (Module 0 onward, all waves) operate at the **product-spec layer**, not the tech-implementation layer. Concretely:
  - **In PRD scope**: business intent and behaviour; entity *concepts* and the business attributes they carry; lifecycle state machines and state names (state names regulate the process and stay in PRD); business-meaningful enum values that define semantics (e.g., a four-value marketing-consent lifecycle); domain event names and the business signals they carry; cross-module dependency contracts and module boundaries; business invariants and gating rules; v17 inheritance citations and qa / DEC traceability.
  - **Out of PRD scope**: JSON / data-shape code blocks; database column types (UUID vs string, decimal precision); FK column naming; nullability flags as schema constraints; indexing and query-pattern decisions; validation-placement claims (application-layer vs schema-layer); event payload field-by-field listings (the *meaning* of payload contents stays in PRD; the exact field names do not). These are tech-team decisions downstream of the PRD.
  - **Balance principle**: where the line is blurred, default to business framing — the tech team is the audience, not the co-author. Examples in spirit:
    - PRD: "translatable per attribute, six launch locales." Tech: JSON-with-locale-keys vs translation table.
    - PRD: "Customer carries marketing-consent lifecycle (none → requested → confirmed via double opt-in → revocable)." Tech: enum value strings + timestamp columns + nullability.
    - PRD: "Originating Club captured at first approval; immutable thereafter; locked via OriginatingClubLocked event." Tech: `Customer.originating_club_id` FK column + nullability + indexing.
  - **Stays in PRD even when it sounds technical**: domain event names (business signals); business-state names (`active`, `sunset`, `closed`); cross-module dependency contracts; v17 inheritance citations; DEC + qa traceability; enum value lists when they regulate the business process (e.g., a four-state membership lifecycle is PRD-level even though "enum" is technical vocabulary).
- **Implications**:
  - **Module 0 + Module K v0.1 PRDs (drafted earlier 2026-05-03)**: revised in place (no version bump — never reviewed) to lift JSON shape blocks, field tables, and schema-constraint prose; concept inheritance + state machines + business event names retained.
  - **All future PRD waves (Module A / S / D / B / C / E)**: drafted from the start at product-spec layer per this DEC.
  - **BMD vs PRD boundary clarified**: BMD = business doc (mechanics, why, scope); PRD = product spec (what the system does in module-internal terms; what events fire; what states matter; what rules apply); tech-design = implementation (JSON, schemas, FKs, indexing, validation placement).
- **Amends / supersedes**: none. Methodology DEC parallel to DEC-060 (PRD inherits v17 by section number, no copy) and DEC-072 (PRD does not take accounting-policy positions). Together, DEC-060 + DEC-072 + DEC-073 define what NewCo PRDs are: inheritance-cited, accounting-neutral, product-spec-layer documents that translate the BMD into module-internal behaviour for the tech team to implement.
- **BMD revision**: none — DEC operates at PRD-drafting methodology layer.
- **Owner**: Paolo.

---

## DEC-074 — NewCo PRDs are self-contained delivery documents; v17 inheritance is audit-trail traceability, not load-bearing prose (2026-05-03)
- **Context**: Surfaced 2026-05-03 in response to Module 0 v0.1 PRD review. v0.1 was drafted strictly per DEC-060 (cite v17 §4 by section number; no copy of v17 prose) and resulted in a divergence-only delta document — readable only alongside an open copy of v17. A tech reader picking up Module 0 v0.1 cold cannot tell what "Three-tier product hierarchy carries forward unchanged per qa.mod0 Q-AD-1" actually *means* without flipping to v17. The cost of strict cite-only inheritance is a non-self-contained delivery doc; the spirit of DEC-073 (PRD = product spec for the tech team to take into the dev phase) requires the document to stand alone. Paolo authorised a v0.2 self-containment pass on Module 0 (and the same pattern on Module K) on 2026-05-03.
- **Decision**: NewCo PRDs (Module 0 onward, all waves) are **self-contained delivery documents**. The load-bearing prose of each module PRD describes that module's entities, lifecycle, governance, business rules, and domain events in NewCo language, top-to-bottom, without requiring the reader to flip to v17 to understand what each entity *is* or what the lifecycle *does*. Concretely:
  - **Self-contained prose body**: every entity carried over from v17 is reintroduced in NewCo language at the level of business concept, business attributes carried, lifecycle states, governance rules, business invariants, and emitted events — sufficient for a tech reader who has not read v17 to take the PRD into the dev phase.
  - **v17 inheritance preserved as audit-trail traceability**: per-section "v17 trace" footnotes or a dedicated inheritance-trace appendix at the end of each module PRD maps each NewCo section to the v17 §X.x anchor + qa atom that confirmed inheritance. The traceability layer remains for audit / diff purposes; it is not the substitute for prose.
  - **No verbatim copy of v17 prose**: rewriting in NewCo language strips Crurated-specific framing, CL-resolution scaffolding ("W4-CL-J", "S-32 Probe A4", etc.), and v17-internal bookkeeping that does not belong in a NewCo delivery doc.
  - **Divergence surfaces still highlighted**: where NewCo strips, simplifies, or extends a v17 pattern, the divergence is called out explicitly (with the underlying DEC + qa atom cited) so the reader can locate the NewCo-specific decision.
  - **DEC-072 + DEC-073 still apply**: self-containment does not relax the no-accounting-policy or no-tech-implementation discipline. The prose stays at product-spec layer with event-only framing throughout.
- **Implications**:
  - **Module 0 v0.1**: stays on disk for audit / diff. Module 0 v0.2 is the delivery doc.
  - **Module K v0.1**: stays on disk for audit / diff. Module K v0.2 is the delivery doc (drafted in a separate window after Module 0 v0.2 lands).
  - **All future PRD waves (Module A / S / D / B / C / E)**: drafted self-contained from v0.1 (no v0.1 → v0.2 self-containment pass needed; the lesson is folded forward).
  - **PRD review by Paolo**: each module PRD is reviewable cold without v17 open alongside.
- **Amends / supersedes**: refines DEC-060. DEC-060 (PRD inherits v17 by section number; v17 prose never copied) is preserved as the **drafting-stage discipline** — the drafter is forbidden from copying v17 prose. DEC-074 sets the **delivery-stage standard** — the drafter must restate inherited patterns in NewCo language so the delivery doc is self-contained. The two DECs operate together: cite v17 by section number AND restate the substance in NewCo prose. Methodology DEC parallel to DEC-060 + DEC-072 + DEC-073. Together, DEC-060 + DEC-072 + DEC-073 + DEC-074 define what NewCo PRDs are: inheritance-cited, accounting-neutral, product-spec-layer, self-contained documents that translate the BMD into module-internal behaviour for the tech team to implement.
- **BMD revision**: none — DEC operates at PRD-drafting methodology layer.
- **Owner**: Paolo.

---

## DEC-075 — Allocation entity unification: single entity for all sourcing-model × visibility combinations (2026-05-04)
- **Context**: Wave 2 Module A elicitation Q-CL-5. NewCo's Allocation universe spans three sourcing models (passive_v1 default, passive_v2, direct_purchase) × two visibility states (CLUB_ONLY, DISCOVERY_ONLY) at launch, with PO timing and pricing semantics differing across the matrix. The data-shape question: single Allocation entity with discriminator attributes vs subtypes per sourcing model vs split tables per visibility. Paolo's qa.mod0 Q-CL-2 follow-through ("all allocations live in Module A regardless of source") strongly endorsed unification.
- **Decision**: NewCo Module A models a **single Allocation entity** at launch. v17 §2.1 inheritance baseline + two NewCo-specific enum extensions (`sourcing_model` per DEC-063; `visibility` per DEC-023) + the conditional pricing fields (DEC-078). All sourcing × visibility combinations live as rows in one entity; conditional-field semantics are routine business validation, not a schema fragmentation surface. No subtypes, no split tables.
- **Implications**:
  - Single FSM (DEC-077 / Q-AD-6 inheritance from BMD §9.6 + v17 §2.1 / §3.1) governs all allocations.
  - Single event set (Q-AD-16) covers all allocations; no per-subtype event proliferation.
  - Reporting / query paths uniform across sourcing × visibility.
  - Composes cleanly with DEC-076 (split-allocation as separate rows, not as a single-entity attribute).
- **Amends / supersedes**: extends DEC-060 inheritance (v17 §2.1 single Allocation pattern preserved); composes with DEC-076 (split realisation), DEC-077 (lifecycle orthogonality), DEC-078 (pricing fields), DEC-079 (mutability scope).
- **BMD revision**: none — entity unification is implementation-shape decision; BMD §3.7 / §4.5 framing already supports.
- **Owner**: Paolo.

---

## DEC-076 — Split-allocation realisation: separate Allocations per visibility, sibling rows from one producer commitment (2026-05-04)
- **Context**: Wave 2 Module A elicitation Q-CL-6. BMD v0.5 §4.5 explicitly defers the data-shape choice for visibility-split commitments (e.g., producer commits 100 units; 80 visible to club at €100, 20 visible to Discovery at NewCo-set price). Two interpretations: (A) one Allocation with `visibility = BOTH` and multiple Module S Offers carving it; (B) two parallel Allocations from one commitment (CLUB_ONLY for 80 + DISCOVERY_ONLY for 20). Paolo overrode the analyst's working answer A in favour of B, with the rationale that the visibility split is a producer-side constraint (Module A scope) with different pricing decision-makers per surface, and the data layer should reflect that separation explicitly.
- **Decision**: NewCo Module A realises visibility-split producer commitments as **separate Allocation rows per visibility** (Interpretation B). One producer commitment of N units that exposes M to club and (N − M) to Discovery materialises as two sibling Allocation rows: one with `visibility = CLUB_ONLY` qty = M and `producer_price` populated; one with `visibility = DISCOVERY_ONLY` qty = (N − M) and `negotiated_cost` populated (DEC-078). Each row carries exactly one pricing field set; pricing decision-maker per row is unambiguous (producer for `producer_price`; producer + NewCo for `negotiated_cost`).
  - **Visibility enum reduced to two values at launch** (`CLUB_ONLY | DISCOVERY_ONLY`); `BOTH` is conceptually inconsistent under this model and is dropped at launch. Future-DEC reactivates `BOTH` if a use case emerges.
  - **Sibling-link**: no explicit FK at launch; producers / NewCo ops aggregate "this came from one commitment" via shared keys (producer_id + BR + sourcing_model + creation timestamp). If sibling tracking complexity grows post-launch, a `parent_commitment_id` UUID can be introduced.
  - **Mid-life rebalancing across siblings**: edit qty on each sibling independently per DEC-079 mutability rules (cannot decrease below issued count); OR mutate visibility on a single allocation to repurpose unsold club stock to Discovery (visibility IS mutable per Q-AD-3 — pricing field flips concurrently per DEC-078). Anti-orphan rule: cannot flip visibility on the unsold-portion of an allocation that has already issued vouchers under the original visibility (those vouchers remain valid under the original commercial relationship); operational pattern for partial repurposing is close-and-spawn.
- **Implications**:
  - **Module S Offer publication**: simpler validation — Offer's surface must exactly match the Allocation's visibility; no `BOTH` ambiguity to resolve at publication time.
  - **Settlement aggregation per row** rather than per commitment: a producer's quarterly settlement statement may contain two rows for what was conceptually "one commitment of 100" — UX layer aggregates by shared keys for display.
  - **Producer Portal + Admin Panel UX** (DEC-083): "create commitment" flow may admit a single-input + auto-split into N sibling rows (UX wrapper); the data layer always sees N rows.
  - DEC-078 pricing-field composition simplified by the single-pricing-field-per-row invariant.
- **Amends / supersedes**: settles BMD v0.5 §4.5 deferred design call. Composes with DEC-075 (entity unification — visibility-split is row-multiplication, not entity multiplication), DEC-078 (pricing fields per visibility), DEC-079 (mutability rules per row).
- **BMD revision**: none required at v0.5 (BMD §4.5 framing accommodates either interpretation; the design call is now made). Optional: §4.5 sentence noting "split commitments materialise as sibling Allocation rows per visibility" can be folded at Wave-2-end v0.6 consolidation if Paolo prefers the BMD body to reflect the chosen shape.
- **Owner**: Paolo.

---

## DEC-077 — Allocation lifecycle orthogonal to ProducerAgreement state transitions (2026-05-04)
- **Context**: Wave 2 Module A elicitation Q-CL-7. DEC-070 locks ProducerAgreement lifecycle (`draft / active / superseded / terminated`) but does not specify whether agreement-state transitions cascade onto child Allocations. Paolo confirmed the transparent / per-allocation-ops interpretation (B) and clarified the underlying cadence asymmetry: ProducerAgreement is a signed legal contract agreed at the start of the producer relationship and effectively static once signed; Allocations are fluid operational units, often email-driven, multiple-concurrent per producer, with their own per-row lifecycle.
- **Decision**: Allocation lifecycle is **orthogonal to ProducerAgreement state transitions**. Agreement transitions to `superseded` (renewal artifact) or `terminated` (off-cycle exit) do NOT auto-cascade onto child allocations. NewCo ops handles per-allocation actions (close, retire, transfer-to-new-agreement) on a case-by-case basis at the moment of agreement state change.
  - **Two cadences explicit**:
    - ProducerAgreement = umbrella legal contract; low-frequency change; regulates clubs / commitment / responsibilities / settlement cadence per DEC-070; transitions are rare.
    - Allocation = per-commitment operational unit; high-frequency creation; informal signaling between producer and NewCo ops; many concurrent per producer.
  - **Rare anomaly path** ("terminated agreement still has active allocations") is a soft alert (operator dashboard), not a schema constraint. Module D Q-AD-4 / DEC (separate, in qa.modD scope) gates PO issuance on agreement state to protect downstream procurement; Module A allocation lifecycle stays uncoupled.
- **Implications**:
  - Allocation FSM (Q-AD-6 / BMD §9.6) operates without agreement-state input; mutability rules (DEC-079) apply uniformly regardless of agreement state.
  - Producer Portal / Admin Panel surfaces (per DEC-083) render the affected-allocations list at the moment of agreement state change for ops-discretionary action.
  - If producer-relationship lifecycle automation matures post-launch, future-DEC may introduce default-cascade rules (auto-close / auto-retire on terminate); not in scope at launch.
- **Amends / supersedes**: composes with DEC-070 (ProducerAgreement entity); refines [`../03-qa/qa.modK.md`](../03-qa/qa.modK.md) Q-AD-9 follow-through implications.
- **BMD revision**: none — orthogonality framing aligns with BMD §3.13 spirit (case-by-case operational handling for rare lifecycle events).
- **Owner**: Paolo.

---

## DEC-078 — Allocation pricing-field composition: `producer_price` (club) + `negotiated_cost` (Discovery + Direct Purchase) (2026-05-04)
- **Context**: Wave 2 Module A elicitation Q-AD-4. Analyst initially proposed `producer_price` (club) + `discovery_cost` (Discovery), with Direct Purchase reading cost from the Module D PO line. Paolo overrode with the framing that Direct Purchase and Discovery should have the SAME pricing-field behaviour — in both cases a per-unit cost is negotiated at allocation time and used in the PO; the only difference is PO timing (V1 → after sale; Direct Purchase → before sale). The `discovery_cost` field is therefore renamed and broadened to `negotiated_cost` with cross-sourcing-model applicability.
- **Decision**: Allocation carries TWO pricing fields:
  - **`producer_price`** — per-unit reference price set by the producer; populated for `visibility = CLUB_ONLY` under `passive_v1 / passive_v2`; used to compute the 12.5% / 87.5% sell-through split per BMD §3.10. The producer-economic model anchors at this field for club allocations.
  - **`negotiated_cost`** — per-unit cost NewCo will pay the supplier / producer; populated for `visibility = DISCOVERY_ONLY` regardless of sourcing model (covers Discovery passive consignment AND Direct Purchase). NewCo sets the customer-facing selling price separately at the Module S Offer level (the cost-vs-price differential is NewCo's Discovery margin). Replaces the prior `discovery_cost` naming.
  - **Field-population by visibility (under DEC-076 single-visibility-per-allocation model)**:
    - `visibility = CLUB_ONLY` + `sourcing_model ∈ {passive_v1, passive_v2}`: `producer_price` populated; `negotiated_cost` NULL.
    - `visibility = DISCOVERY_ONLY` (any sourcing model): `negotiated_cost` populated; `producer_price` NULL.
  - **PO timing (orthogonal to which pricing field is populated)**: V1 → PO after sale (sell-through-driven); V2 → PO at sell-through-settlement cadence (financial PO against pre-positioned stock); Direct Purchase → PO at allocation/purchase time (before sale). Cross-link to Module D Q-AD-3 PO timing.
  - **Direct Purchase + CLUB_ONLY**: not a launch use case (Direct Purchase per BMD §3.7 is positioned as a Discovery exception); not forbidden by the data model but expected null-volume at launch.
  - **Visibility mutation cascades to pricing field** (per DEC-076): flipping CLUB_ONLY → DISCOVERY_ONLY also flips `producer_price` → null and populates `negotiated_cost` (renegotiated at flip-time). Atomic update operation surfaced from Producer Portal + Admin Panel per DEC-083.
- **Implications**:
  - Each allocation row carries exactly one of `producer_price` OR `negotiated_cost` populated (not both). Field-population validation lives in business logic per DEC-073 (no schema-constraint claims in PRD).
  - Module D PO line read: for V1/V2 club, PO references `producer_price` × qty (less producer settlement portion); for Discovery / Direct Purchase, PO references `negotiated_cost` × qty.
  - Sell-through settlement event payload (Q-AD-12) carries the relevant pricing-field value for downstream Module E.
- **Amends / supersedes**: refines and renames the `discovery_cost` field originally proposed under DEC-061 / DEC-032 framing; composes with DEC-075 (entity unification) and DEC-076 (split realisation per visibility).
- **BMD revision**: optional — BMD §3.10 prose currently uses `C` (Discovery cost) and `P` (club price) symbolic notation; an Appendix A Glossary note clarifying `negotiated_cost` covers both Discovery passive-consignment and Direct Purchase can be folded at Wave-2-end v0.6 consolidation.
- **Owner**: Paolo.

---

## DEC-079 — Allocation mutability generalised beyond Hero Package: `qty` mutable across all sourcing × visibility combinations (2026-05-04)
- **Context**: Wave 2 Module A elicitation Q-AD-7. DEC-069 locks mid-year `Allocation.qty` mutability for Hero Package allocations specifically; the qa atom asked whether the same mutability generalises to non-Hero club allocations, Discovery allocations, and Direct Purchase allocations. Paolo confirmed Option X (generalise to all allocation types).
- **Decision**: `Allocation.qty` mutability generalises to **all sourcing × visibility combinations** at launch. The DEC-069 mechanic (mutate `qty`; cannot decrease below issued voucher count = anti-orphan rule) applies uniformly across passive_v1, passive_v2, and direct_purchase sourcing models, and across CLUB_ONLY and DISCOVERY_ONLY visibilities.
  - **Waitlist-conversion side-effect remains club-specific** (per Module K v0.2 §13 + DEC-069 mechanic): when a club allocation's `qty` increases, the producer is offered N waitlisted applicants in priority order to approve. Discovery and Direct Purchase allocations have no waitlist concept; capacity increase simply makes more inventory available for sale.
  - **Direct Purchase capacity increase** implies a follow-on PO to the supplier per Module D Q-AD-3 timing (additional PO at-purchase-time for the new units).
  - **Anti-orphan rule** (cannot decrease `qty` below issued voucher count) applies uniformly across all types.
  - **Producer-breakability immutability** (Q-AD-8 / v17 §3.4) is NOT extended by this DEC; `producer_breakability` remains immutable post-first-voucher-issuance regardless of `qty` mutability.
- **Implications**:
  - `AllocationCapacityIncreased` and `AllocationCapacityDecreased` events (Q-AD-16) fire uniformly across allocation types.
  - Mutation surfaced from Producer Portal + Admin Panel per DEC-083 (Club owners not engaging with the Producer Portal can have NewCo ops mutate `qty` from the Admin Panel).
  - Consistent UX framing: "scale the allocation" is one operation regardless of channel.
- **Amends / supersedes**: generalises DEC-069 from Hero-Package-only to Allocation-wide. DEC-069 remains the canonical statement for Hero-Package-specific waitlist mechanics.
- **BMD revision**: optional — BMD §2.3 mid-year capacity sentence (already added at v0.4 consolidation per DEC-069 BMD revision clause) currently anchors on Hero Packages; a parallel sentence in §3.7 / §3.9 generalising "allocation `qty` is mutable across sourcing models" can be folded at Wave-2-end v0.6 consolidation.
- **Owner**: Paolo.

---

## DEC-080 — Non-serialization opt-out extended to all allocations (club + Discovery + Direct Purchase); per-producer choice, not visibility-gated (2026-05-04)
- **Context**: Wave 2 Module A elicitation Q-AD-10. DEC-052 originally framed non-serialization opt-out as a Discovery-specific exception (producer or NewCo opt-out per allocation for Discovery surface). Paolo clarified that some producers reject NFC serialization on principle and the flexibility must be admitted at the producer-relationship level for ALL allocations — including club allocations — not gated by visibility.
- **Decision**: Non-serialization opt-out is admissible across **all allocations at launch** (any sourcing × visibility combination). Allocation carries a `non_serialized_offer_admitted` boolean (default FALSE — serialization-by-default per BMD §6.1 stands); producer can opt out at allocation creation regardless of visibility, mutating the flag to TRUE. The flag is per-allocation, not per-producer (one producer may opt-in for some allocations and out for others; e.g., the producer's Hero Package allocation may be serialized while a year-round normal allocation is not).
  - **Sub-pool partition mechanics** (`qty_to_serialize` / `qty_non_serialized` numerics + pre-issuance rebalance + post-issuance not-yet-issued-only mutation) carry forward unchanged.
  - **DEC-052 framing broadened**: was Discovery-allocation opt-out; now any-allocation opt-out. DEC-052's substance is preserved; only the scope is widened.
- **Implications**:
  - Producer Portal + Admin Panel (per DEC-083) expose the opt-out toggle on every allocation creation surface, not gated by visibility.
  - Module S Offer-publication validation (Wave 3 Module S scope): an Offer attempting `serialization_type = NON_SERIALIZED` must be backed by an Allocation with `non_serialized_offer_admitted = TRUE`; previously this validation was Discovery-specific, now it applies to club Offers too.
  - Module B (Wave 4 — NFC / NFT) inherits the broadened scope: club bottles may also be non-serialized at the producer's choice; the predecessor / successor recovery chain (BMD §6.11) applies only when serialization is in effect.
  - Bottle Page (DEC-053) read pattern: serialized vs non-serialized framing is per-Offer / per-Allocation; the customer-facing UX label clarifies the distinction.
- **Amends / supersedes**: broadens DEC-052 scope; composes with BMD §6.1 default-on policy (preserved).
- **BMD revision**: required at Wave-2-end v0.6 consolidation. BMD §6.1 framing currently anchors the "non-serialized exception" on Discovery; revise to "non-serialized exception is admissible across all allocations on producer opt-out". DEC-052 entry in §12.1 table also broadens its scope description.
- **Owner**: Paolo.

---

## DEC-081 — Direct Purchase Allocation FSM: DRAFT → ACTIVE on `SupplierPaymentCompleted`, NOT on physical receipt (2026-05-04)
- **Context**: Wave 2 Module A elicitation Q-AD-13. The cross-cut between Module A (Allocation FSM) and Module D (PI / PO timing) under Direct Purchase (DEC-063) initially read "goods inbound to NewCo before Allocation moves to ACTIVE." Paolo flagged that for Direct Purchase the Allocation should become ACTIVE earlier — sales can start before goods are physically received; physical availability is needed only for shipments. He proposed "after the PO is completed (or producer paid)" as the canonical trigger.
- **Decision**: For Direct Purchase Allocations, the **DRAFT → ACTIVE transition fires on `SupplierPaymentCompleted`** (Module D event), NOT on `InboundEventPhysicallyAccepted`. Rationale: NewCo's financial commitment is the binding economic act (cash leaves NewCo); past that point the inventory is contractually NewCo's regardless of in-transit status; sales can proceed; physical receipt is a downstream operational dependency for shipment, not for sellability.
  - **Decoupled gates**:
    - **Sellability gate** (Module S Offer publication / voucher issuance against the allocation): `Allocation.state = ACTIVE` — for Direct Purchase = supplier payment completed.
    - **Shipment gate** (Module C fulfilment): `InboundEventPhysicallyAccepted` for the relevant qty — gates physical shipment, not voucher issuance.
  - **In-transit voucher UX**: Module C / Module S surface displays "in transit; ETA X" on vouchers awaiting physical receipt; customer can place orders against ACTIVE allocations whose goods are not yet at NewCo. Acceptable customer-experience trade for the cash-flow / time-to-market gain.
  - **V1 / V2 unchanged**: passive consignment Allocations go ACTIVE upon producer commitment + setup (no upfront payment); PI fires at voucher issuance; PO at sell-through-cadence per DEC-070. The DRAFT → ACTIVE trigger refinement is Direct-Purchase-specific.
  - **Trigger choice — payment vs PO-issued**: payment-completed is the canonical trigger (cash-binding) rather than PO-issued (which doesn't bind cash); aligns with Paolo's "or producer paid" framing.
- **Implications**:
  - Module D Q-AD-1 (PI inheritance + Direct Purchase divergence) and Q-AD-3 (PO timing per sourcing model) recommendations refreshed post-Q-AD-13 to reflect ACTIVE-on-payment trigger.
  - Module A Q-AD-6 FSM (BMD §9.6 + v17 inheritance) carries an inline note that the DRAFT → ACTIVE trigger is sourcing-model-conditional: V1/V2 = producer-commitment-completed; Direct Purchase = supplier-payment-completed.
  - Cash-flow model: NewCo pays Direct Purchase suppliers at-PO and exposes the inventory to Discovery sales immediately; cash recovery cycle (sale → customer payment → NewCo cash) starts before physical inbound completes.
  - Module C fulfilment must gracefully handle "voucher exists but goods not yet physically here" — display ETA on customer order page; ship when InboundEvent.PHYSICALLY_ACCEPTED fires.
- **Amends / supersedes**: refines DEC-063 (Direct Purchase mechanic) — adds the ACTIVE-on-payment trigger detail. Composes with DEC-070 (ProducerAgreement settlement cadence — does not apply to Direct Purchase per DEC-063) and DEC-072 (event-only framing — `SupplierPaymentCompleted` is the trigger event, accounting treatment downstream).
- **BMD revision**: optional but recommended at Wave-2-end v0.6 consolidation. BMD §3.7 / §5.1 prose around Direct Purchase can add a sentence: "Allocation is sellable from `SupplierPaymentCompleted`; physical receipt gates shipment only." Aligns BMD body with the FSM trigger.
- **Owner**: Paolo.
- **Stage 6.5 clarification (2026-05-08, E6-32 Path 2 — superseded by DEC-183)**: The DRAFT → ACTIVE trigger for Direct Purchase has been **harmonized with V1 / V2 to "operator-publish post-PO-commit"** per DEC-183. ACTIVE is uniformly defined as "Allocation is sellable" across sourcing models. `SupplierPaymentCompleted` remains a Module D / E financial event recording supplier payment but no longer drives Allocation FSM. Supplier-payment-failure on Direct Purchase becomes a financial-recovery scenario (operator queue + customer refund per DEC-104 + DEC-165), not an FSM-state mismatch. The "Voucher ISSUED on DRAFT Allocation" gap window dissolves at the FSM layer (Voucher issuance can no longer occur on a DRAFT Allocation by construction). Original DEC-081 body (above) preserved verbatim; this clarification supersedes the FSM-trigger framing only. See DEC-183 for the harmonization framing.

---

## DEC-082 — Allocation counterparty: `producer_id` always; `supplier_id` optional, common on Discovery, admitted on Club (2026-05-04)
- **Context**: Wave 2 Module A elicitation Q-AD-14. Analyst recommendation framed `supplier_id` population as "rare" (typically Crurated-as-Supplier or holding-company exceptions). Paolo refined: for Discovery it will be COMMON to enter into commercial relationships with Suppliers to source allocations of wines made by N producers; Crurated is one such Supplier; for Club allocations the general rule is no Supplier, but Producer-with-long-established-Supplier-relationship is ADMITTED ("get the Club allocation from that Supplier").
- **Decision**: Allocation carries a **two-FK counterparty pattern**:
  - **`producer_id`** — always populated; FK to Module K §4.4 Producer (the wine identity, "who made it"); read by sell-through settlement, Wine Master deref, audit.
  - **`supplier_id`** — optional; FK to Module K §4.5 Supplier (the commercial counterparty, "who NewCo paid"). Population frequency:
    - **Discovery (CLUB_ONLY = N/A; DISCOVERY_ONLY)**: COMMON. Discovery Suppliers (Crurated being one example; others expected as NewCo grows the Discovery surface) hold allocations spanning N Producers; each constituent allocation references its producer_id + the shared supplier_id.
    - **Club (CLUB_ONLY)**: ADMITTED (rare but supported). Producer may delegate sourcing to a long-established Supplier; data model supports from launch even if operational frequency is low.
  - **Settlement / PO routing**: routes to `supplier_id` when populated; falls back to `producer_id` when null.
  - **SupplierProducerLink** (Module D Q-AD-9 — DEC TBD in qa.modD scope) gates PO line items in BOTH the common Discovery+Supplier case AND the admitted Club+Supplier case. The link entity is operationally authoritative for "is this Supplier authorised to ship this Producer's wine?"
- **Implications**:
  - **Supplier-allocation often spans N Producers**: a Discovery Supplier holding an allocation of wines from multiple Producers materialises as N parallel Allocations (one per Producer × Wine Variant) per DEC-076 split-realisation pattern, each with own `producer_id` + shared `supplier_id`.
  - **Discovery + Supplier is the operational norm at launch**, not the exception — recommendation prose framing in Module A PRD must reflect this.
  - **Club + Supplier path** validates the DEC-067 separation discipline (Producer ≠ Supplier) at the data layer even under low operational frequency.
  - Module D Q-CL-9 (Crurated-as-Supplier sourcing model) and Q-AD-9 (SupplierProducerLink validation) framing refreshed to reflect Discovery+Supplier as common-not-rare.
- **Amends / supersedes**: refines DEC-067 (Producer ≠ Supplier separation) application in Module A. Composes with DEC-020 (Crurated as Discovery Supplier — operational from day one).
- **BMD revision**: optional. BMD §3.1 currently frames producer-as-counterparty as the default; a clarifying sentence noting that Discovery commonly transacts with Suppliers-not-Producers (one or many Producers per Supplier) can be folded at Wave-2-end v0.6 consolidation.
- **Owner**: Paolo.

---

## DEC-083 — Producer Portal ↔ Admin Panel parity for per-allocation operations (2026-05-04)
- **Context**: Wave 2 Module A elicitation Q-AD-17. While confirming Option Y for unsold-stock-handling (no `unsold_handler_policy` field; Producer Portal triggers per-allocation actions), Paolo flagged a cross-cutting operational principle: not all Club owners will operate the Producer Portal at launch; some prefer email + ops support; the NewCo Admin Panel must be functionally complete on per-allocation operations for those producers.
- **Decision**: NewCo locks **Producer Portal ↔ Admin Panel parity** as a cross-cutting design principle for Module A operations. Every allocation-level operation is exposable from BOTH surfaces:
  - **Producer Portal**: producer-facing; Club-owner-self-service.
  - **NewCo Admin Panel**: NewCo-ops-facing; acts on behalf of producers (especially Club owners not engaged with the Portal).
  - **Operations covered**: visibility mutation (DEC-076), qty mutation (DEC-079), pricing-field updates (DEC-078), recall trigger (Q-AD-17), sub-pool rebalancing + non-serialization opt-out toggle (DEC-080), allocation creation, allocation lifecycle transitions (CLOSE / RETIRE), counterparty assignment (DEC-082).
  - **Audit trail**: every allocation-level event (Q-AD-16 set) carries the actor (`actor_role: producer | newco_ops`) so the source of the action is traceable.
  - **State propagation**: NewCo ops actions in the Admin Panel propagate state to the Producer Portal so the producer view stays consistent if/when they engage.
- **Implications**:
  - **Wave 3 (Module S)**: same parity principle likely extends to Offer-level operations (Producer Portal Offer-creation surface ↔ Admin Panel Offer-creation surface). Flag for Wave 3 elicitation.
  - **Wave 2 Module A PRD drafting**: every operation described as "actor: Producer (Portal) OR NewCo Ops (Admin Panel)"; surface-specific UX is downstream tech work per DEC-073.
  - **Wave 4 / Wave 5 cross-cuts**: Module B (NFC / NFT) and Module C (fulfilment) operations may have similar parity needs (e.g., NFC re-issuance triggered by ops or producer); Wave 4 elicitation to surface.
- **Amends / supersedes**: cross-cutting principle, no prior DEC affected. Composes with DEC-073 (PRD scope = product-spec layer, surface-specific UX downstream) and DEC-074 (PRDs are self-contained delivery docs).
- **BMD revision**: none — operational/UX principle that does not require BMD body revision; will be referenced inline in PRDs.
- **Owner**: Paolo.

---

## DEC-084 — SupplierAgreement entity deferred at launch; supplier commercial terms live at allocation level (2026-05-04)
- **Context**: Wave 2 Module D elicitation Q-CL-8. Three-position fork on whether Module D needed a parallel `SupplierAgreement` entity to mirror Module K §4.6 ProducerAgreement. Paolo confirmed Option C (defer entity at launch) with the framing that the supplier agreement is "purely commercial" and that "working commercial terms need to be present at allocation level".
- **Decision**: **No SupplierAgreement entity at launch.** Module D reads informal Supplier metadata from Module K Supplier (Party `party_type = SUPPLIER`). Supplier-counterparty commercial terms (cost shape, payment terms) live on the **Allocation entity**, not on a separate agreement entity. Two-tier conceptual model:
  - **ProducerAgreement (Module K §4.6)** = club-relationship UMBRELLA. Required for any Producer-counterparty transaction.
  - **Per-allocation commercial terms** (Allocation entity) = SPECIFIC commercial terms for that allocation (cost shape, payment terms). Composes with Q-CL-9 reshape (commercial-terms shape independent of sourcing model and counterparty type).
  - **Module K Supplier** carries informal metadata at launch: optional `payment_terms`, `notes`. Field set is light; growth to a SupplierAgreement entity is a Phase-2+ option if Supplier relationships diversify (multi-year terms, settlement statements, exclusivity).
- **Implications**:
  - Module D PRD: no SupplierAgreement entity in the data-model section; PO line items reference the Allocation for commercial terms + Module K Supplier for counterparty metadata.
  - Cross-link DEC-070 (ProducerAgreement is Module K's umbrella, not Module D's per-allocation construct).
  - Q-AD-4 PO gating model (HELD pending Paolo confirmation) leverages this two-tier distinction: ProducerAgreement gates Producer-counterparty POs at the umbrella level; per-allocation state gates the specific PO regardless of counterparty type.
- **Amends / supersedes**: no prior DEC affected; refines Q-CL-8 recommendation.
- **BMD revision**: none — no BMD body claim about SupplierAgreement entity exists; Module D PRD scope only.
- **Owner**: Paolo.

---

## DEC-085 — PurchaseOrder ownership 3-value enum: PRODUCER / NEWCO / THIRD_PARTY; ownership derives from Allocation.sourcing_model (2026-05-04)
- **Context**: Wave 2 Module D elicitation Q-AD-2. Confirmation of v17 §8 PO entity inheritance with the NewCo-specific rename of the CRURATED ownership enum value to NEWCO; ownership derives from Allocation.sourcing_model at PO creation.
- **Decision**: PurchaseOrder entity inherits v17 §8 verbatim. The `ownership` 3-value enum (per Crurated v17 lineage memory `project_ownership_flag_model`) carries forward as **PRODUCER / NEWCO / THIRD_PARTY** at NewCo (renamed from CRURATED → NEWCO).
  - **Ownership derivation rule** at PO creation reads Allocation.sourcing_model:
    - `direct_purchase` → ownership = NEWCO at PO issuance.
    - `passive_v1 / passive_v2` → ownership = PRODUCER through sell-through; transitions to NEWCO (or directly to customer per fulfilment path) at sell-through-settlement / shipment per BMD §3.10.
  - **THIRD_PARTY** reserved for future use (e.g., consignee-not-NewCo paths).
- **Implications**:
  - Module D PRD: ownership 3-value enum + derivation rule documented; PRODUCER / NEWCO / THIRD_PARTY tokenisation locked.
  - Cross-module reads (Module C fulfilment, Module E events) reference the same enum; rename CRURATED → NEWCO applied consistently across NewCo PRDs.
- **Amends / supersedes**: aligns Crurated v17 ownership-enum naming to NewCo-tokenisation. No prior DEC affected.
- **BMD revision**: none — BMD doesn't currently use the CRURATED token; PRD rename suffices.
- **Owner**: Paolo.

## DEC-086 — PurchaseOrder timing three-way model + cross-module event chain SupplierPaymentCompleted → AllocationActivated (2026-05-04)
- **Context**: Wave 2 Module D elicitation Q-AD-3. Confirmation of three-way PO timing model branching on sourcing model + the Direct-Purchase-specific cross-module event chain (Module D `SupplierPaymentCompleted` → Module A `AllocationActivated` per DEC-081).
- **Decision**: PO timing branches on `Allocation.sourcing_model`:
  - **V1 (passive consignment, customer-order-driven)**: PI auto-fires at voucher issuance (one PI per voucher in simple case; batched per shipment in optimised flow); PO issues against the PI per the producer's ProducerAgreement settlement cadence (Module K §4.6, DEC-070). PO is a goods-movement PO that ships from producer.
  - **V2 (passive consignment, pre-positioned)**: PI fires at voucher issuance (referencing already-arrived stock); PO issues at sell-through-settlement cadence per ProducerAgreement. PO is a financial PO against pre-positioned inventory, not a goods-movement PO.
  - **Direct Purchase**: PO issues at PI creation time (operator-initiated, before Allocation moves to ACTIVE); PO is full-amount-at-purchase financial commitment; supplier payment completion fires Module D `SupplierPaymentCompleted` event; Module A reads that event and fires `AllocationActivated` (DRAFT → ACTIVE) per DEC-081. Allocation is sellable from this point — physical receipt (`InboundEventPhysicallyAccepted`) gates Module C shipment only.
- **Implications**:
  - Module D PRD: three-way timing rule + the `SupplierPaymentCompleted → AllocationActivated` cross-module event chain documented.
  - Module A PRD reads this DEC's Direct-Purchase-trigger contract (already locked in DEC-081).
  - Module C handles "voucher exists but goods not yet physically here" gracefully (display ETA on customer order page; ship when InboundEvent.PHYSICALLY_ACCEPTED fires).
- **Amends / supersedes**: composes with DEC-063 (Direct Purchase as third sourcing model), DEC-070 (settlement cadence per ProducerAgreement), DEC-081 (Allocation FSM Direct-Purchase trigger).
- **BMD revision**: none — BMD §3.7 / §3.10 already anchor the timing-by-sourcing-model framing; PRD-level documentation of the cross-module event chain suffices. DEC-081 BMD revision (optional Wave-2-end §3.7 / §5.1 sentence) covers the "Direct Purchase ACTIVE-on-payment" surface.
- **Owner**: Paolo.
- **Stage 6.5 clarification (2026-05-08, E6-32 Path 2 — superseded by DEC-183)**: The cross-module event chain `SupplierPaymentCompleted → AllocationActivated` has been refined per DEC-183. `AllocationActivated` is now triggered by **operator-publish post-PO-commit** (uniform across V1 / V2 / Direct Purchase per DEC-183); `SupplierPaymentCompleted` remains a downstream Module D / E financial event but does not drive Allocation FSM. The three-way PO timing model (V1 / V2 / Direct Purchase) is preserved verbatim in DEC-086 above; only the FSM-trigger composition is reframed. Original DEC-086 body preserved verbatim; this clarification supersedes the Direct-Purchase FSM-trigger framing only.

---

## DEC-087 — Module D owns SupplierProducerLink entity; PO-line validation gate at issuance (2026-05-04)
- **Context**: Wave 2 Module D elicitation Q-AD-9. Module D owns the SupplierProducerLink entity (N:N between Supplier and Producer per DEC-067), with PO-line validation at issuance time that an active link exists between the PO Supplier and each line's BR's Producer.
- **Decision**: Module D owns the **SupplierProducerLink** entity:
  - **Shape**: N:N link entity between Module K Supplier (`party_type = SUPPLIER`) and Module K Producer (§4.4); lifecycle `active / inactive`.
  - **Creation rule**: operator-explicit (per v17 §8.10's no-auto-link rule); no auto-creation on producer or supplier onboarding.
  - **PO-line validation gate**: at PO issuance, every PO line item validates that an active SupplierProducerLink exists between the PO's Supplier and the line's BR's Producer (BR → Wine Master → Producer deref). Validation failure blocks PO issuance.
  - **Module K dependency**: Module K owns the underlying Supplier and Producer entities (per qa.modK Q-CL-4); Module D owns the relationship-binding entity.
  - **Producer-as-Supplier collapse**: when Producer = Supplier (Producer's Party row carries `party_type = SUPPLIER` in addition to `party_type = PRODUCER` per Module K v0.2 patterns), the SupplierProducerLink is self-referential and materialises at producer onboarding.
- **Implications**:
  - Module D PRD: SupplierProducerLink entity in data-model section; PO-line validation rule documented.
  - Cross-module reference: Module K v0.2 §4.4 (Producer) + §4.5 (Supplier) cited; Module D PRD writes the link entity.
  - Discovery-with-Supplier-not-Producer (DEC-082 common pattern): validation gate ensures the Discovery Supplier is authorised for each constituent Producer's wine in the allocation.
- **Amends / supersedes**: composes with DEC-067 (Producer ≠ Supplier separation) and DEC-082 (two-FK counterparty pattern).
- **BMD revision**: none — BMD doesn't claim the entity; Module D PRD scope.
- **Owner**: Paolo.

---

## DEC-088 — Inbound-receiving party = Supplier always; Producer-as-Supplier collapses trivially (2026-05-04)
- **Context**: Wave 2 Module D elicitation Q-AD-10. Inbound-receiving party (the entity from whom NewCo receives goods at InboundEvent / ConsignmentReceipt time) is by default the Supplier (PO counterparty); for the Producer-as-Supplier case the Producer is also the Supplier so the collapse is trivial. Recommendation refreshed post-DEC-082 to reflect Discovery+Supplier as the COMMON operational pattern, not a rare exception.
- **Decision**: Module D's inbound-receiving party is **always the Supplier** (Module K Party `party_type = SUPPLIER`), the PO counterparty:
  - **Producer-as-Supplier case** (Producer's Party row carries both `party_type = PRODUCER` and `party_type = SUPPLIER`): the Producer is also the Supplier; the receiving party is the Producer trivially.
  - **Discovery-with-Supplier-not-Producer case** (the COMMON Discovery operational pattern per DEC-082): inbound routes through the Supplier counterparty.
  - **Club-with-Supplier case** (admitted per DEC-082, lower frequency): producer-delegated Supplier as receiving party.
  - **Producer-ships-direct-without-Supplier-of-record**: operationally rare (typically agency-model territory NewCo doesn't run at launch); out of Wave 2 scope.
- **Implications**:
  - Module D PRD: data model treats every PO + InboundEvent as having a Supplier counterparty; the receiving-party derivation reads PO.supplier_counterparty.
  - Cross-link: qa.modK Q-CL-4 (Producer-as-Supplier collapse pattern) + DEC-082 (two-FK counterparty pattern).
  - Validates the DEC-067 Producer ≠ Supplier separation discipline at the inbound-event level.
- **Amends / supersedes**: composes with DEC-067 + DEC-082.
- **BMD revision**: none — BMD §3.1 producer-as-counterparty default carries forward; the receiving-party operational rule lives at PRD level.
- **Owner**: Paolo.

---

## DEC-089 — INV1 / INV2 customer-facing only; Supplier payment shape domain-separated (2026-05-04)
- **Context**: Wave 2 Module D elicitation Q-AD-13. Direct Purchase Supplier payment shape vs the customer-facing INV1 / INV2 two-invoice mechanic (DEC-045) — explicit separation lock to avoid future confusion.
- **Decision**: The **INV1 / INV2 two-invoice mechanic (DEC-045)** is **customer-facing only** (NewCo's invoice to the customer; INV1 at checkout for goods value, INV2 at shipment with excise + VAT). It does **NOT** apply to Supplier-counterparty payments.
  - **Supplier payment shape** (Direct Purchase + any sourcing model with Supplier counterparty): single financial commitment at PO issuance (PO unit price × qty + landed-cost adjustments per Q-AD-7 / DEC-072 event-only framing); payment to Supplier follows Supplier's payment terms (net 30 / net 60 / etc., from informal Supplier metadata per DEC-084).
  - **Domain separation**: customer-facing invoicing (INV1/INV2) governs how NewCo invoices the customer (excise + VAT timing); Supplier payment governs how NewCo pays the Supplier (per PO + Supplier's payment terms). Two distinct domains, two distinct entity / event sets.
- **Implications**:
  - Module D PRD: explicit separation called out to prevent future PRD drafting drift conflating the two domains.
  - Module S PRD (Wave 3) reads INV1/INV2 mechanic at customer-facing checkout/shipment timing; Module D PRD reads `SupplierPaymentCompleted` at Supplier-facing PO timing.
- **Amends / supersedes**: composes with DEC-045 (INV1/INV2 customer-facing) and DEC-063 (Direct Purchase mechanic) and DEC-084 (Supplier metadata at launch).
- **BMD revision**: none — BMD §5.4 INV1/INV2 mechanic is already customer-facing-framed; PRD documents the domain separation.
- **Owner**: Paolo.

---

## DEC-090 — Producer recall reverse-inbound: Module D event-recording at launch + manual operator capability admitted (2026-05-04)
- **Context**: Wave 2 Module D elicitation Q-AD-14 + Q-OQ-12. Producer recall of unsold V2 consignment goods (BMD §3.9 path); v12 acknowledged the capability but mechanics unmodeled (memory `project_v12_consignment_recall_gap`). Q-AD-14 lands the minimal Module D event-recording role at launch; Q-OQ-12 confirms full mechanics deferred BUT requires manual operator capability at launch.
- **Decision**: Module D records `ReverseInboundEventRecorded` event for producer-initiated unsold-V2-goods recall at launch:
  - **Event payload**: which Allocation, which goods (BR + qty), which destination (return-to-Producer), which trigger (producer-initiated recall via Producer Portal per qa.modA Q-AD-17, OR manual operator entry via NewCo Admin Panel per DEC-083).
  - **Manual operator capability at launch**: NewCo Admin Panel surfaces a "record producer recall" action; operator inputs the event payload; event fires; downstream Module C handles physical reverse logistics (operationally manual at launch); downstream Module E backs out cost-basis recognition (per DEC-072 event-only framing).
  - **Full reverse-inbound mechanics deferred to Phase 2+** per Q-OQ-12: reverse 3-gate QC (mirror of inbound), reverse cost-basis unwind precision (partial-recall accuracy, multi-event netting), partial-recall UX, recall-dispute path, automated return-shipment carrier coordination, reverse-discrepancy paths.
- **Implications**:
  - Module D PRD: `ReverseInboundEventRecorded` event in event catalogue; manual operator capability documented; full mechanics flagged as Phase 2+ deferred.
  - qa.modA Q-AD-17 cross-link: Producer Portal triggers the recall (DEC scope is Module A); Module D records the resulting event.
  - Phase 2+ extension: when triggered, Module D extends with reverse-inbound entity model (analogous to InboundEvent two-phase but mirrored: PHYSICAL_RETURN_ACCEPTED → COST_REVERSAL_FINALIZED).
- **Amends / supersedes**: addresses the v12-acknowledged gap (`project_v12_consignment_recall_gap` memory); composes with BMD §3.9 (producer discretion on unsold-stock handling) and DEC-083 (Producer Portal ↔ Admin Panel parity).
- **BMD revision**: none — BMD §3.9 already acknowledges the capability; PRD lands the minimal event + manual operator capability.
- **Owner**: Paolo.
